These were some of the scariest moments in my life. Everybody we crossed
 here was mad at us. We sent our coordinates to the home front every 10 
minutes or so. <br>
<br>
Relentlesly we continued. It got pitch dark and the road was really 
difficult. We could not afford to make mistakes now, but we also did not
 feel like getting out of the car to inspect any obstacles. The dark was
 actually good for us as people would not see that we are white. This 
seemed to make a major difference in the reaction of the people.<br>
<br>
But we made it. We were so happy to reach Kananga and at the same time 
scared to death that people would react the same here. Fortunately the 
town was quiet and actually looked friendly in the moonlight. Due to 
pure luck we drove straight into the compound of the procure and at that
 into safety.<br>
<br>
The friendly father-abt allowed us to camp in the garden. He looked 
genuinely surprised if we told him about our bad experience but at the 
same time it was as if he was avoiding the subject too.<br>
<br>
We put up the tent, got out our chairs and opened one of our "emergency 
beers". We just sat there a long time without saying a word to 
eachother. The sky was beautiful and the sounds of all the insects was 
magnificent.</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">So, what was that all about?<br>
<br>
In all honesty, we don't have a clue! I only know that this ranks very 
high in my top 10 scariest moments. Everybody has their limits, well 
this was over mine. I do not want this to happen to me again.<br>
<br>
- Where we just panicking for no reason, paranoid by all the 
(mis)information we received? Did we create the danger in our minds?<br>
<br>
Maybe, I really can't tell. We discussed this afterwards, and we did not
 make up those mobs that charged at us. They had machetes. They did 
chase us. <br>
<br>
We have a few theories though:<br>
<br>
- These villages were on a newly created "detour". Normally no motorized
 traffic would pass trough here. Bicycles only. Maybe they saw this as 
new way to generate money, and they wanted their part of the cake. 
Although somebody should explain to them that this is not a good way to 
ask for a toll fee.<br>
<br>
- We had the feeling that they were focussing on us, not only because we
 were in a vehicle, but because of our skin color. Did a white person do
 something wrong here? Where they trying to seek vengeance? I wouldn't 
surprise me if a white person in car ran somebody over, or destroyed 
something and then fled away.<br>
<br>
- Some fetish reason. Witchdoctors have a lot of influence here. If they
 had casted a spell of some sorts. Or predicted that something bad would
 happend if a white person would pass trough here.<br>
<br>
- ...<br>
<br>
I guess we will never know.</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">Progress after day 12. Kananga<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-1-1587032570" data-lb-id="_xfUid-1-1587032570">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-1-1587032570" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/congo_democratic_republic_map-day12.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/congo_democratic_republic_map-day12.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/congo_democratic_republic_map-day12.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div></div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">Thanks for the kind words Christian and others.<br>
<br>
Regarding OLJ, how does one get an article in there? Not sure if this 
story is apropriate for publishing in magazines, I have no idea how to 
make this any shorter without it losing the 'vibe' it requires.</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><b>Day 13</b><br>
<br>
This was the half way point and up until now we at least had minimal 
information on what was ahead of us. That would end here. The only thing
 we knew was that the bac (ferry) at Tshikapa was not working - 
confirmed here in Kananga - and that the road to Tshikipa was not only 
suspect for "coupeurs de route" but also in a horrible state (mud!).<br>
<br>
The alternative was to go north from here to Ilebo were apparantly there
 was a ferry. And worst case we could try to put the car on a boat on 
the Congo river to Kinshasa. Nobody here in Kananga had gone all the way
 to Ilebo by car. Until about halfway there were some missions, but they
 were considered 'cut off' due to the state of the roads. Especially the
 last part of the road into Ilebo was said to be impossible.<br>
<br>
But most of it was hearsay anyway. People don't travel much overland here.<br>
<br>
We were halfway and it looked like what we just did was the easy part... <br>
<br>
Yesterday's events had gotten us exhausted and we decided to stay for a 
day in the safetey of the procure. We tried to get some sleep and do 
some cleaning up in the car. I also had to tape/bolt various bits and 
pieces back to the car.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-1-1587032581" data-lb-id="_xfUid-1-1587032581">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-1-1587032581" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/ilebo001.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/ilebo001.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/ilebo001.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
Staying at the procure also gave us the opportunity to meet some 
interesting people. They also had their own radio station. Because they 
had a huge antenna this was one of the most important radio stations in 
the area. For a lot of people the radio was their only means of 
information from the outside world. They were well equipped and the 
radio crew was young and extremely motivated.<br>
<br>
They did an interview with us, but we asked them not to air the 
interview immediately but instead wait 4 days. If it would be aired 
immediately it would be a matter of minutes before the entire police 
force came for their "share". Also with yesterdays events in the back of
 our mind, we wanted to keep the aspect of surprise.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-2-1587032581" data-lb-id="_xfUid-2-1587032581">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-2-1587032581" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/ilebo004.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/ilebo004.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/ilebo004.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div></div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><b>Day 14</b><br>
<br>
Kananga looked like a beautiful - but rundown -city, but we did not 
really visit anything. At this point we just wanted to stay low profile 
and keep moving. <br>
<br>
We set of direction Ilebo, not knowing what to expect. The roads has a bit of an erosion problem<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-3-1587032581" data-lb-id="_xfUid-3-1587032581">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-3-1587032581" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga064.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kananga064.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga064.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
On the above picture you can clearly see where our axle was touching the middelmanetjie.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-4-1587032581" data-lb-id="_xfUid-4-1587032581">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-4-1587032581" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga065.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kananga065.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga065.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
This was all jolly good if both tracks erored equally. This was not 
always the case and we got into a habit of driving at some extreme 
angle. Often scraping the sidewalls.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-5-1587032581" data-lb-id="_xfUid-5-1587032581">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-5-1587032581" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga069.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kananga069.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga069.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-6-1587032581" data-lb-id="_xfUid-6-1587032581">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-6-1587032581" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga068.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kananga068.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga068.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
How long ago was it that road was actually "up there" where the grass is.</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">As
 said, traffic is always local. They somehow manage to get cars into 
larger towns and then drive it around town, but no trough traffic. So 
cities/towns/village that are not on a river or on the limited railroad 
network have very limited supplies.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-7-1587032581" data-lb-id="_xfUid-7-1587032581">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-7-1587032581" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga070.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kananga070.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga070.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
Up to 600kg of goods are transported on these bicycles. They do not 
'ride' them, but push them instead. You can see there is a stick 
connected to the bikes handlebars. <br>
<br>
This is the major transport method in Congo. It is probably one of the 
most 'popular' (this does not seem like a good wordchoice) jobs. There 
are fixed routes and people often travel in groups. For security reasons
 but also to help eachother on the hills. <br>
<br>
At regular intervals on the main "bicycle" tracks there are "service 
stations". This is usualy a small hut where one can eat a meal of fufu. 
They would also have a pump and some basic tools to fix flats.<br>
<br>
We saw many of these overloaded bicycles before, but on this stretch of 
the road it seems to be the only means of transportation.<br>
<br>
It must be very hard work to get these loads over the sometimes very 
rough roads. The 'drivers' are away from home for weeks on end and 
probably barely make any money out of it.<br>
<br>
We never had problems with these guys, they were much to busy with their job.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-8-1587032581" data-lb-id="_xfUid-8-1587032581">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-8-1587032581" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga071.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kananga071.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga071.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-9-1587032581" data-lb-id="_xfUid-9-1587032581">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-9-1587032581" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga072.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kananga072.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/kananga072.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
This also meant we were no longer driving on real roads. But on bicycle tracks...</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><blockquote class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeBlock--expandable bbCodeBlock--quote">
	
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-title">
			
				<a href="file:///forum/goto/post?id=737837" class="bbCodeBlock-sourceJump" data-xf-click="attribution" data-content-selector="#post-737837">LaOutbackTrail said:</a>
			
		</div>
	
	<div class="bbCodeBlock-content">
		
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandContent ">
			Could it be that some of those roads were old rail road beds? It 
seems as if many of the "bridges" you crossed were constructed of train 
rails?
		</div>
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandLink"><a>Click to expand...</a></div>
	</div>
</blockquote>Until now we mostly followed the Route National 1, which 
used to be a real road (dirt). Although some of the original parts 
probably no longer exists. Detours ar formed when the road gets 
impassible and sometimes the detours then become the main road. The only
 railway they even built here still exists and connects Kananga and 
Lubumbashi. I think train rails just made for a convenient building 
material. Many of the bridges have been fairly recently (20 years ago?) 
rebuilt by the missions.<br>
<br>
So no, I do not think these road we rail road beds.<br>
<br>
With regards to questions about our vehicle: fire away. Our website contains a fair amount of information on the car too: <a href="http://www.radiobaobab.be/" target="_blank" class="link link--external" data-proxy-href="/forum/proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.radiobaobab.be&amp;hash=2988e5c4addb3c68fbe6d9db677d587e" rel="nofollow noopener">www.radiobaobab.be</a>
 , then click on the UK flag (top right) for the English version and 
then choose "The car" in the menu. Our website is terribly outdated and 
due to get an update and revamp.<br>
<br>
Our car is a simple affair compared to some of the rigs on this forum. But it worke very well for us.</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">Some notes from Josephine (posting and reading from the same account as Frederik)<br>
<br>




<blockquote class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeBlock--expandable bbCodeBlock--quote">
	
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-title">
			
				Frederik Willems said:
			
		</div>
	
	<div class="bbCodeBlock-content">
		
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandContent ">
			We tried to sneak in the village but failed miserably. Same thing 
happened again, confused looks at first, as soon as they saw us they 
shouted at eachother and then came storming after us.
		</div>
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandLink"><a>Click to expand...</a></div>
	</div>
</blockquote>What surprised me was that it were not just men, but also women who were shouting.<br>
<br>




<blockquote class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeBlock--expandable bbCodeBlock--quote">
	
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-title">
			
				Frederik Willems said:
			
		</div>
	
	<div class="bbCodeBlock-content">
		
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandContent ">
			We sent our coordinates to the home front every 10 minutes or so.
		</div>
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandLink"><a>Click to expand...</a></div>
	</div>
</blockquote>Afterwards we heard that Frederik's mom and dad followed 
our progress on Google Earth in real time. The idea that somebody knew 
where we were was a relief to us.</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">We 
were pretty optimistic and hoped to reach Ilebo in two days. That meant 
that on the first day we had to make it to Pembeyangu, were we knew of a
 mission.<br>
<br>
Bicycle tracks are not suited for Landcruisers... so we got stuck. The 
villages usually had the worst obstacles. In this one village there was a
 big boghole filled with water. We drove in but did not see the pigs 
that were taking a bath so we slowed down to give them the time to get 
out.<br>
<br>
Big mistake. We were stuck. The water came to the bottom of the door. 
This particular mudpit had a bit of a funny smell. It was the favourite 
place of the pigs so it probably contained a fair amount of sh*t. It 
sure smelled like it. The entire village gathered round us while we got 
out, knee deep in sh*t.<br>
<br>
They did not offer help.<br>
<br>
We started clearing the wheels. Josephine hurt her foot on a stick, the 
pain could be seen on her face. The people thought this was extremely 
funny and burst out laughing. This was very humiliating for Josephine 
and I could see the anger on her face. We looked at eachother and 
understood that this was not the time to get angry or start discussions 
with 50 or so people. We continued to work. As I bend over to clear the 
mud from underneath the car my pants get wet up until my ehrm.. 
'privates'.. . Once again this is the funniest thing these people have 
ever seen. Hilarity ensues. This was very humiliating to us.<br>
<br>
Eventually they offered to help us if we pay them. I tell them that I do not have money. They did not move an inch.<br>
<br>
It takes the best part of an hour to get us out. To their surprise we 
stop again and I get out and walk up to them. Very calmly I explain that
 we did not like it when they laughed at us. I asked them how they would
 react if they hurt themselves and we would laugh at them. The 
acknowledged that they would get mad at us.<br>
I asked them if they would want us to help them if they had a problem. 
The acknowledged this. I said what they would think if we asked for 
money before we would help them. They called us racists and immediately 
demanded money from us.<br>
<br>
I then saw a side of Josephine I hadn't seen before. She got very cross 
with words and gestures. I will not repeat what she said here... it 
wasn't pretty I must say  8O Much to the amusement of our adience.<br>
<br>
To some of the people in the village our message must have gotten along, and they guided us around the next boghole. <br>
<br>
Half an hour later we stopped to eat lunch. We were still shaking after the humiliation, we felt helpess.<br>
We opened a can of Coke (still from Zambia) and a jar of pickled onions to eat with our bread.<br>
<br>
Those 'horrible' people did not have a Coke, even if they had the money 
to buy it, it was not avaialble. They did not have pickled onions 
either. And between the two of us we ate as much bread as an entire 
family would eat for an entire day.<br>
<br>
We tried putting things into perspective. Maybe we shouldn't be here after all?<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-1-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-1-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-1-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu007.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/pembeyangu007.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu007.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
That is not the same pit/people from the above anecdote, but it is very 
similar. We must have crossed 20 or so villages like this.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-2-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-2-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-2-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu008.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/pembeyangu008.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu008.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div></div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">The progress we hoped to be making today did not materialize.. <br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-3-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-3-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-3-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu011.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/pembeyangu011.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu011.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
This was the thoughest going we had thus far since we left Lubumbashi. 
While the road had always been difficult, the inbetween bits used to be 
ok. Those inbetween bits did no longer exist now. The erosian was pretty
 bad and we were creeping forward<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-4-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-4-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-4-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu009.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/pembeyangu009.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu009.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
Every obstacle meant a new dent or other damage<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-5-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-5-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-5-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu012.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/pembeyangu012.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu012.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
To make matters worse we drove straight into a tropical storm..</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><blockquote class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeBlock--expandable bbCodeBlock--quote">
	
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-title">
			
				<a href="file:///forum/goto/post?id=738596" class="bbCodeBlock-sourceJump" data-xf-click="attribution" data-content-selector="#post-738596">nat said:</a>
			
		</div>
	
	<div class="bbCodeBlock-content">
		
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandContent ">
			What means did you two have to defend yourselves should the need have arisen?
		</div>
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandLink"><a>Click to expand...</a></div>
	</div>
</blockquote>A sense of humour and patience.<br>
<br>
And if that doesn't work, a quick pair of legs ;-)</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><blockquote class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeBlock--expandable bbCodeBlock--quote">
	
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-title">
			
				<a href="file:///forum/goto/post?id=738600" class="bbCodeBlock-sourceJump" data-xf-click="attribution" data-content-selector="#post-738600">LaOutbackTrail said:</a>
			
		</div>
	
	<div class="bbCodeBlock-content">
		
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandContent ">
			All things considered and "treading lightly" out the window.... why not make a new path around some of these bogs?
		</div>
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandLink"><a>Click to expand...</a></div>
	</div>
</blockquote>That is what we did when possible. But we did not take 
pictures of that ;-) Often the jungle was to dense, or the ridges to 
steep to drive around obstacles. We tried to avoid obstacles as much as 
possible.</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">In a fast pace the clouds 
appeared out of nowhere, in a matter of minutes it became as dark as the
 night. Winds picked up and jungle forest made terrible noise. Thick 
drops started banging on our car. Slowly at first but exponentially 
growing in size and number. Lightning almost immediately followed by 
deafening thunder. The hard rain stirred the ground and released many 
smells.<br>
<br>
God, I love those tropical storms! A little less today though, as the 
track we were driving on quickly became very mudy. The ruts filled with 
water and became streams. Visibility was down to nil as our windscreen 
wipers couldn't keep up.<br>
<br>
This slowed us down even more. We slid and slide.. sideways more then forward.<br>
<br>
We came to another village, refreshingly we had the road for us alone, 
as everybody had taken cover for the rain. The usual bogholes were 
present but we could drive around it... or could we?<br>
<br>
What looked like a viable bypass was nothing more then a meter thick 
layer of soft and sticky mud on top of a puddle. Our landcruiser sunk in
 deep.<br>
<br>
I got out and within seconds I was drenched, I could barely breath 
because of the water that ran down my face and into my mouth. This was 
useless I couldn't see a thing. We had to wait until the rain stopped.<br>
<br>
Luckily those tropical storms go as quickyl as they come and after an 
half hour wait the downpour transformed in a little drizzle.<br>
<br>
We have gotten ourselves properly stuck I must say. Up unto the axles. 
Out came the sandplates and the shovels and I started digging. The 
village too had noticed the rain had resided and quickly came to see 
what was going on.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-7-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-7-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-7-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu005.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/pembeyangu005.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu005.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
No surprisingly nobody they offered their assistance, they even had some
 shovels. But they wanted money first. By now you probably think we are 
just stupidly stubborn and naive. We probably are, but we refused to 
give in to corruption. I once again told them they were free to help, 
but we would not give them money. So I continued to dig on my own with 
an entire village as an audience.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-8-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-8-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-8-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu006.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/pembeyangu006.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/pembeyangu006.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
It took three more attempts to drive out before the village priest (7th 
day Adventist by the way) encouraged a few strong men to help. After a 
small discussion between the priest and the men they helped us 
eventually. We did not promise them anything. Good!<br>
<br>
Almost two hours after we drove in we succesfully managed to back out. 
The priest then lead us trough his village (milimeterwork between the 
huts) around the bogholes.<br>
<br>
We offered the priest a small fee for his spontaneous help. We were 
grateful. He was in trouble now as he had to split up the money between 
the helpers and we could see a discussion had started already.<br>
<br>
Covered in mud we continued... the hope to get to Pembeyanga today has long vanished. Darkness was starting to fall...</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">We
 were a in a miserable state. We were both soaked and there was mud 
everywhere, exhausted and stirred by todays experiences. Hungry. And 
above all nervous as to where we would stop for the night. We passed a 
few villages, they looked very poor and rundown. On the GPS we saw we 
were nearing a somwhat larger settlement: Kakenge. In the dark we did 
another 5km (about an hour).<br>
<br>
Kakenge was indeed a large settlement and our luck turned as not only 
was there a catholic mission, it was a nice catholic mission! A fenced 
of compound (2 meter high walls.. who were they trying to keep out?) 
with inside a beautiful garden and two simple but clean buildings. The 
only brick buildings in town. Four fathers lived here, all Congolese but
 most of them had studied abroad. One of the fathers, Frère Polydore, 
had lived in Rome for 8 years. He had the humour and the way of talking 
of an Italian, a funny guy. They let us camp, have a shower (bucket) and
 they even let us use their dining room in all peacefulness.<br>
<br>
Just what we needed! Today we spent 15 hours on the road in our struggle forward. What a day...<br>
<br>
They also gave us the news that the road to Ilebo would progressively get worse and even impassable...</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">Progress after day 14. Kakenge<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-9-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-9-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-9-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/congo_democratic_republic_map-day14.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/congo_democratic_republic_map-day14.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/congo_democratic_republic_map-day14.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div></div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><b>Day 15</b><br>
<br>
We slept until late today and only got on the road at 9. Silently we 
hoped to reach Pembeyangu today although the road would have to better 
as yesterday.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-10-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-10-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-10-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo007.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo007.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo007.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-11-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-11-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-11-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo006.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo006.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo006.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
The road was not better then yesterday.<br>
<br>
Erosion became a real problem and we spent most of our time "underground"<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-12-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-12-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-12-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo010.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo010.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo010.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-13-1587032592" data-lb-id="_xfUid-13-1587032592">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-13-1587032592" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo011.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo011.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo011.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
And then we tipped over...</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">Thank you so 
much for all the kind words. It is a great feeling to know we are not 
boring you guys with our little trip report here ;-)<br>
<br>




<blockquote class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeBlock--expandable bbCodeBlock--quote">
	
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-title">
			
				<a href="file:///forum/goto/post?id=738837" class="bbCodeBlock-sourceJump" data-xf-click="attribution" data-content-selector="#post-738837">blazinid said:</a>
			
		</div>
	
	<div class="bbCodeBlock-content">
		
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandContent ">
			I notice your bullbar seems to be winch ready.  Do you not have a 
winch on the truck?  Seems it would come in handy with all the bogs you 
get stuck in!
		</div>
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandLink"><a>Click to expand...</a></div>
	</div>
</blockquote>Nope, no winch. We would have used it often if we had one, 
but at when we were preparing for the trip we could choose between 
buying a winch, or an extra month on the road. We went for the extra 
month.<br>
<br>
A winch can be handy, but there is always an alternative. Sometimes it meant it takes days to get out, instead of minutes.</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">We
 had been driving in akward angles a lot, and a few times already we 
could feel two wheels lifting off, but until now we managed to always 
end up on our 4 wheels. Until now..<br>
<br>
We had two wheels in the air and we were resting on our side. Luckily 
the eroded sidewall made sure we did not fall too deep. We knew it would
 happen sooner or later but the sound of bending sheetmetal still scared
 us a bit.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-3-1587032603" data-lb-id="_xfUid-3-1587032603">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-3-1587032603" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo016.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo016.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo016.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
It was nothing spectacular (sorry  <img src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" class="smilie smilie--sprite smilie--sprite10" alt=":oops:" title="Oops!    :oops:" data-shortname=":oops:">
 ) but nevertheless, we were in a situation were our wheels were 20 cm 
off the ground. We do not have locking differentials by the way.<br>
<br>
We got our shovel out again  :roll: and starting to add ground 
underneath our wheels to make them grip again and made the next few 
meters a bit more level hoping that we would righten ourselves again. It
 worked like a charm but it was a great amount of work. Damage was 
limited to a few extra dents.<br>
<br>
Still exhausted we continued, still in bizarre angles.<br>
<br>
Then we tipped over again..</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">"Annoyed" 
would be a correct word to describe our mood. We could still see were we
 tipped over last time and we knew how much digging it takes to get the 
car righted again.<br>
<br>
No choice... out came the shovel... and eventually we got out again... 
and it did not take another kilometer before we... tipped over again... 
and again..<br>
<br>
And again.<br>
<br>
At this rate it would take years to get us to Ilebo, we had to find a 
way to keep moving. Now, most of the road was ok to drive on. The little
 indicator on our dashoard learned us that we could keep driving until 
about 35 degrees tilt angle. It were only occasional patches were the 
angle would become too big and we'de be on our sides.<br>
<br>
We figured that if we would keep enough momentum, that we would slide 
forward on our side and "bounce back" on our wheels. So, that is what we
 did. We kept the speed up and if the road dipped too much we would tip 
over. Because of the higher speed the impact on the side was much 
bigger. But that, combined with the forward movement created a "jo-jo" 
effect (do you guys know what a jo-jo is? Not sure if it is called the 
same in English).<br>
<br>
Move forward. Tip over. Slide forward a bit on the side of the car. 
Bounce back. Wheels touch the ground. Move forward. And repeat.<br>
<br>
Some of the longer steep section were maybe 100meter long. We would 
"bounce" numerous times to get trough this. When we got trough we had a 
fixed procedure:<br>
<br>
- Depending on what side we tipped over, the person sitting on the opposite side would get out of the car first.<br>
- Armed with a hamer and spanner "20" go to the other side of the car<br>
- Bang and bend the door back into shape so it would open again<br>
- Both of us would walk back the part we just "bounced" trough, picking 
up all the parts of the car that fell of. Usually the mirrors, various 
bits and pieces of the filling cap, the sandladders, indicator lights 
and the odd bits of our roofrack.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-4-1587032603" data-lb-id="_xfUid-4-1587032603">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-4-1587032603" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo017.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo017.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo017.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-5-1587032603" data-lb-id="_xfUid-5-1587032603">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-5-1587032603" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo018.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo018.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo018.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-6-1587032603" data-lb-id="_xfUid-6-1587032603">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-6-1587032603" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo019.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo019.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/548/naarilebo019.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
Strong car!<br>
<br>
This technique is probably not described in any "4x4 driving techniques" handbook.  :wink:</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">That
 day we did the "tip over thing" at least 20 times. After a while you 
stop worrying about the dents, but I can still hear the sound of the 
impacts.<br>
<br>
Then, out of the blue, there was a road! This was completely absurd, as 
this road led to nowhere, but here it was, a recently build road about 
10 meters wide. The forest was cut and cleared, the ground was made 
level and smooth as silk  8O <br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-7-1587032603" data-lb-id="_xfUid-7-1587032603">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-7-1587032603" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo021.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo021.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo021.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
Where did this come from?<br>
<br>
We drove onto the road and immediately started sinking in. I floored it 
to keep momentum and we crept forward, leaving deep ruts behind us.<br>
<br>
We felt really bad when that happened. Somebody put a huge amount of 
effort in building a road here. And then comes along this stupid tourist
 and he just pulls two big ruts spot in the middle of this road.<br>
<br>
We did not stay around to take a picture of our ruts, we were a bit embarrased.<br>
<br>
The road dissapeared as suddenyl as it appeared before.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-8-1587032603" data-lb-id="_xfUid-8-1587032603">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-8-1587032603" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo022.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo022.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo022.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
What the ... ?</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><blockquote class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeBlock--expandable bbCodeBlock--quote">
	
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-title">
			
				<a href="file:///forum/goto/post?id=739549" class="bbCodeBlock-sourceJump" data-xf-click="attribution" data-content-selector="#post-739549">constructeur said:</a>
			
		</div>
	
	<div class="bbCodeBlock-content">
		
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandContent ">
			I've reviewed your website and I'm still curious of a few things. 
These questions apply to all your travels, not just this trip.<br>
<br>
How do you and Josephine get on with washing clothes? and if they need 
drying (If it's the rainy season and you can't rely on the sun or dry 
heat)
		</div>
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandLink"><a>Click to expand...</a></div>
	</div>
</blockquote>If we stayed at a campsite and had running water, we did 
the wash there. When you travel for a long time, you regularly stay 
somewhere for a few days to get organized again. Sometimes we were "on 
the go" for a longer period of time, then we washed up in rivers or 
whatever was available. We did this immediately after stopping at night.
 If it wasn't dry in the morning, we hung some bungees in the back of 
the car. We probably had a permanent grubby look though.<br>
In DRC it was a lost case. The humidity, the mud, the digging. We looked
 -and smelled - like we got stuck in the jungle for two months! ;-)<br>
<br>




<blockquote class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeBlock--expandable bbCodeBlock--quote">
	
	<div class="bbCodeBlock-content">
		
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandContent ">
			How are you cooking?
		</div>
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandLink"><a>Click to expand...</a></div>
	</div>
</blockquote>Started out with a Coleman two pit gasoline burner. Great 
piece of kit, but after 9 months of dirty African fuel it was really 
finished. Everything was black black black, bad burning, etc.. Barely 
useable. In Japan we bought the same stove again. Seconhand. That one 
was shot after 6 months of dirty Russian fuel. We then ordered a Primus 
Omnifuel and had it shipped to Cairo. A bit more work to set up, and 
only one pit. But it worked. After 6 months we had to rebuild the entire
 stove, but it is still functional now.<br>
<br>




<blockquote class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeBlock--expandable bbCodeBlock--quote">
	
	<div class="bbCodeBlock-content">
		
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandContent ">
			How is your car interior outfitted?
		</div>
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandLink"><a>Click to expand...</a></div>
	</div>
</blockquote>Some pictures from during the buildup can be found here: <a href="http://radiobaobab.be/index.php?id=178" target="_blank" class="link link--external" data-proxy-href="/forum/proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fradiobaobab.be%2Findex.php%3Fid%3D178&amp;hash=d10357961483ac28f0b4ee1e35ee93de" rel="nofollow noopener">http://radiobaobab.be/index.php?id=178</a>
 . We could sit inside in emergencies or if it was really cold. It was 
ok, but on the long cold evenings it was a bit cramped. In the warm 
countries we lived outside ofcourse.<br>
Everything homemade on the interior.<br>
<br>




<blockquote class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeBlock--expandable bbCodeBlock--quote">
	
	<div class="bbCodeBlock-content">
		
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandContent ">
			Could you also include something of items or tools you wish you had, and things you installed and don't use that much.
		</div>
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandLink"><a>Click to expand...</a></div>
	</div>
</blockquote>Phew, difficult question. I once formulated a better and 
more detailed answer for this, but I can't really remember. You can soon
 read it in Chris Scott's new book (Overland Handbook) which is due for 
publication <br>
In short: we used everything we took and didn't miss anything we didn't 
take. Which does not mean we really 'needed' everything we took.</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><blockquote class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeBlock--expandable bbCodeBlock--quote">
	
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-title">
			
				<a href="file:///forum/goto/post?id=739601" class="bbCodeBlock-sourceJump" data-xf-click="attribution" data-content-selector="#post-739601">grahamfitter said:</a>
			
		</div>
	
	<div class="bbCodeBlock-content">
		
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandContent ">
			When you were busy digging, did you think you should have bought a 
winch instead of some other things you bought for the trip? Or would you
 have preferred to leave them behind, too, for another extra month on 
the road?
		</div>
		<div class="bbCodeBlock-expandLink"><a>Click to expand...</a></div>
	</div>
</blockquote>When we were busy digging we thought of only one thing: 
getting out of the obstacle, using whatever was available. Thinking 
about the things that we did not have but could have helped us at the 
time would have been a sure recipe to get a depression.<br>
<br>
But yes, it did cross our mind. And yes, it would have helped 
tremendously and reduced the damage the our car (the value of all the 
things we broke exceeds - by far - the price of a winch). But did we 
need it? Nope, we have always gotten out this far without a winch<br>
<br>
But given the option, I would choose the month extra any time.<br>
<br>
That said, I am building a new and improved version and a winch is on my shopping list.. but only if we have some spare cash..<br>
<br>
Then again, there is something magical about getting trough impossible 
obstacles. The improvisation, the stress, the hard labour.. Great stuff!
 A winch would kinda spoil the fun ;-)</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-3-1587032614" data-lb-id="_xfUid-3-1587032614">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-3-1587032614" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo030.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo030.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo030.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
The road was pretty varied. Jungle track. 'Bouncing track', weird 
patches of newly constructed road, etc.. I am not sure which kind of 
road we liked more... or disliked more.. . Often we had to wait to let 
the bicycles pass, sometimes they had to wait to let us pass.<br>
<br>
Not surprisingly we would not make it to Pembeyangu today either. They 
gave us too much hope in Kananga that we could make it in one day. It 
was obvious that nobody there had recently travelled on this stretch. Or
 maybe they had travelled it on foot or on a bicycle, and they do not 
have a clue how difficult this road is with 4 wheels instead of 2.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-4-1587032614" data-lb-id="_xfUid-4-1587032614">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-4-1587032614" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo035.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo035.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo035.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-5-1587032614" data-lb-id="_xfUid-5-1587032614">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-5-1587032614" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo012.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo012.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo012.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
We stopped in the biggest 'town' in the area, Domiongo. It took a bit of
 searching to find a cathalic mission, it was on the outskirts of the 
villlage. Once again we were greeted friendly and had permission to camp
 in their grounds. We sat together with the fathers and talked for many 
hours. <br>
<br>
They told us about the mysterious roads. Apparently some NGO (they did 
not know the details... or they told the details and we forgot) has 
funded the construction. Several teams started working at several 
locations. The different bits were supposed to connect at one point. As 
of recent, work had nearly stopped... no more budget. It was unclear if 
more budget would become available or not. In any case the idea of the 
construction was to invest all the money in labour instead of buying an 
expensive CAT. Great idea ofcourse, that way all the money stayed in 
DRC, instead of filling the pocket of some bigwig at CAT. If you look at
 the road it was quite a feat. They thought about drainage and 
everything. Unfortunately they could not compress the earth enough with 
the tools they had. We already started a few ruts, it would only take 1 
heavy truck to completely destroy these roads again. These roads would 
not last a rainy season.<br>
<br>
The major complaint of the fathers was the upcome of all sorts of other 
religious movements (we talked about 7th day adventists before, but 
other movements were active in the area too). They claimed that they 
grew in popularity because of the animated ceremonies. But these 
movements did not have the social network and organisation behind them 
as the catholic missions. People would no longer work at the farm of the
 mission, would drop out of school, etc... Apparantly 'alternative' 
religions were also gaining in poularity, like fetishism, ..<br>
<br>
Anyway, we talked about many other things too, it was a pleasant evening with interesting people.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-6-1587032614" data-lb-id="_xfUid-6-1587032614">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-6-1587032614" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo033.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo033.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo033.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
In the evening the fathers would run their generator for a few hours. It
 was in a little hut very close to our tent. The hut was half submersed 
from the rain water.  All of a sudden the generator shorted. Smoke and 
blue lightning came out of the hut. One of the fathers ran in the hut, 
barefoot (!), with a stick and hit the offending cable until it got 
disconnected. Brave father!</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">Progress after day 15. Domiongo.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-7-1587032614" data-lb-id="_xfUid-7-1587032614">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-7-1587032614" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/congo_democratic_republic_map-day15.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/congo_democratic_republic_map-day15.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/congo_democratic_republic_map-day15.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div></div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">We came across a small 
motorcycle. You'd see them from time to time, it is the most luxurious 
transportation people have here. They are litte chinese 50cc (or 125cc) 
bikes. We stopped to let him pass and he stopped to greet and ask us if 
we had some oil for his engine.<br>
<br>
All over the world there is an unwritten rule that in remote or 
difficult to travel areas people help eachother. That is why in the 
sahara everybody says hi to eachother. That is why in the Mongolian 
steppe people drive for kilometers just to check up on you. People help 
when needed as they know they will be helped when they are in need. We 
very much honour this unwritten rule and will always assist when we can.<br>
<br>
So when this guy asks for oil, I do not hesitate and take out a my spare
 can of oil. I warn him that this is oil for diesel engines, but that 
does not matter to him. It is probably the best oil he would ever find 
to put in his little bike. As I am pouring oil from my can in his can 
the passenger of the bike starts begging with Josephine. I am not 
impressed when Josephine tells me. And when the bike owner too start to 
ask for money, it really pisses me off. We are helping this guy and 
still he begs for more? So I pour the oil out of his can back into mine 
and tell them to sod off. In our car and off we go.<br>
<br>
For almost a month now we were in a serious fight with Congo. We were 
fighting against corruption. We were fighting against the roads. A 
constant battle. Congo was giving us a serious beating, but we stood 
strong and did not give in. Slowly but steadily we were winning this 
battle against the Congo.<br>
But while we were so busy battling the roads and the corruption, Congo 
sneaked in from behind. It had transformed us into loud and angry 
people. With no remorse, no compassion, and a total lack of rules.<br>
<br>
What happened to the unwritte rule of the road less travelled? The rule we nohour so much? All out of the door..<br>
<br>
Congo had beaten us a long time ago already. Just like it had beaten most of its own citizens.. And we didn't have a clue</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-1-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-1-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-1-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo029.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/naarilebo029.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/naarilebo029.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
The road from Kananga to Ilebo goes mostly trough forest, but Pembeyange
 is situated on top of a hill in a beautiful plain. Really pictoresque. <br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-2-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-2-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-2-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kananga%20074.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kananga%20074.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kananga%20074.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
Upon our arrival in the (small) village everybody went completely nuts. 
Children cheered and ran after us, we had our usual crowd again. As they
 guided us trough the village towards the mission it showed that people 
here do not have notions about cars. They led us between huts, trough 
gardens, ... This was the way they always took to walk to the mission, 
but they failed to see that this was impossible with a car. As we did 
not want drive over peoples houses we backtracked and had to find 
ourselves another route to the mission. In the meantime the children had
 great fun climbing on our wheelcarriers. The wheelcarriers are not made
 for this kind of weight and one of them broke off... great! This was so
 much fun that the now targetted the other wheelcarrier. Josephine had 
to walk behind the car to keep the kids off.<br>
<br>
Unfortunately the father of this mission was not there, but his 
apprentice was. A very young guy, fresh out of school. He was not happy 
to be here, that much was clear. He did nothing else but complain and he
 would whine on endlessly. He was not a bad guy, but was wan't very good
 company either.. oh well.<br>
<br>
The mission had a small toilet hut. A hole in the ground affair with a 
roof on top, the roof was very low, which made it difficult to 'do your 
thing'. When Josephine made use of the facilities she could hear 
something rustling in the roof. When she look up she was face-to-face 
with a thin green/brown snake. I had never seen Josephine run so fast! 
From her description it could have been a green mamba? When told to the 
'maman' who took care of the mission she too was scared and with great 
care she chased the snake a way. "Très dangereux" apparantely.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-3-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-3-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-3-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo001.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo001.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo001.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-4-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-4-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-4-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo004.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo004.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo004.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div></div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">Progress after day 16. Pembeyangu<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-5-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-5-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-5-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/congo_democratic_republic_map-day16.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/congo_democratic_republic_map-day16.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/congo_democratic_republic_map-day16.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div></div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><b>Day 17</b><br>
<br>
It is only 50 kilometers to Ilebo from here. <br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-6-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-6-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-6-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo006.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo006.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo006.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-7-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-7-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-7-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo007.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo007.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo007.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-8-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-8-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-8-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo009.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo009.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo009.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-9-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-9-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-9-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo013.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo013.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo013.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-10-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-10-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-10-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo014.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo014.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo014.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div></div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">We came across a truck that was 
parked in the middle of the track. Luckily the surrounding area was 
pretty open, so we could pass it.<br>
<br>
Us: "Bonjour, ca va?" - "Hi, how are you?"<br>
- Them: "Ca va un peu bien " - "I am doing a little bit ok" -&gt; typical Congelese answer this!<br>
<br>
Us: "Votre vehicle est en panne?" - "Did you truck broke down?"<br>
- Them: "Oui, mais ils vient avec des nouveaux pièces" - "Yes, but they are coming with spare parts"<br>
<br>
So we chat a bit and we ask what their problem exactly was. They left 
Ilebo for Kananga with a load of building materials for a rich guy in 
Kananga. Their engine had completely seized. Their cargo was transferred
 onto another truck and they had taken the engine out and transported 
the engine to Kinshasa to get it rebuild. In the meantime the truck 
'crew' stayed onsite to safeguard the truck. But they were very happy as
 they just received news that the necessary parts for the engine were 
now ordered in Germany, so the parts would come arrive in Kinshasa in a 
few weeks time!<br>
<br>
A fascinating story, and they told it as if the was the most normal 
thing in the world. Fair enough. We said our goodbyes and asked them one
 more final question. How long had they been here?<br>
<br>
"Un peu plus qu'un an maintenant" - "Just over a year"</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-11-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-11-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-11-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo015.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo015.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo015.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-12-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-12-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-12-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo016.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo016.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo016.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-13-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-13-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-13-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo024.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo024.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo024.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
The following pictures were from within the car when we just tipped 
over. As it happened again we were just sitting still for a minute 
before getting into action again. The kids would curiously  came and see
 why this car was on its side, and why the passengers wouldn't come out.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-14-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-14-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-14-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo026.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo026.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo026.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-15-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-15-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-15-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo027.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo027.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo027.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
And then they would ask for money.</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">The 
rest of the day we spent mostly underground... and quite a lot of time 
was spent on our sides. Got stuck a few times and our spade saw some 
hours of work today.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-16-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-16-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-16-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo017.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo017.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo017.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-17-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-17-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-17-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo018.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo018.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo018.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-18-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-18-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-18-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo019.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo019.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo019.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-19-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-19-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-19-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo020.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo020.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo020.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-20-1587032625" data-lb-id="_xfUid-20-1587032625">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-20-1587032625" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo021.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo021.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo021.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
We were too exhausted to be happy that we could finally see Ilebo in the
 distance. We knew nothing about the city. We would have to arrange a 
ferry here to get across the Kasai river. Or worst case, arrange a barge
 to Kinshasa.</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">Hi uk4x4, if you don't 
mind, I am going to wait with my answer to that question until later in 
the report. You'll understand when we get there ;-)</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">Our
 exhaust broke of just at the exhaust manifold. Probably due to to all 
the flexing on these roads. All hopes of arriving somewhere without 
getting noticed were out of the door with that.<br>
<br>
Quite to our surprise there was no checkpoint at the entrance of Ilebo. 
But actually that is not too strange, as nobody ever takes that road. 
Ilebo has a bustling harbour city feel about it. Lots of activity on the
 streets. We got a lot of stares, but people seemed friendly. <br>
<br>
We headed straight for the catholic mission and were greeted by Abbé 
Omer. The mission was the former headquarters of Belgian sisters 
(Josephites?). They had fled a the country a few times, and after the 
last war they did not return. The building was given to the Catholic 
mission. It looked like a nice building, but the decay had started.<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-1-1587032636" data-lb-id="_xfUid-1-1587032636">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-1-1587032636" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo031.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/kabombo031.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/kabombo031.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div>

<br>
<br>
We discussed our plans with Abbé Omer in the garden of the mission (it 
must have been a wonderfull garden back in the days.. now it looked a 
bit rundown). The good news was that there was good ferry here that 
could take us across the mighty Kasai river. The bad news was that 
nobody every uses that ferry and it does not see any regular action.<br>
<br>
Omer knew the guy who was responsible for the Ferry, a chap called 
Barthélémy. He even has his phone number, but he does not have credit on
 his phone. No problem, he can use ours. A conversation in Lingala 
starts, it takes about ten minutes until we run out of credit on our 
phone. I actually think they talked 1 minute about the ferry and the 
other 9 minutes about other things, but anyway. Here was the deal:<br>
<br>
- Price for a two-way trip is 50$US<br>
But, <br>
- we have to supply our own diesel the engine of the boat. 150 liters is
 required (!). that's about 200$US (Diesel here is cheaper because they 
have a regular supply via boats from Kinshasa).<br>
- we have to supply two batteries to start the engines of the boat<br>
- the ferry is on the other side of the river and they would only be able to get it across somewhere next week<br>
<br>
That's just great!<br>
<br>
We immediatelly uttered to Omer that that was a ridiculously high price,
 one we would never pay. And that we wanted to cross as soon as 
possible. preferably tomorrow.<br>
<br>
What followed was a very difficult negotiation. Abbé Omer insisted that 
he acted as an intermediate person. According to him to protect us from 
getting ripped off (because we were white). I was actually convinced 
that he was playing a game with his mate Barthélémy to make some money 
out of us. It took us many hours on the phone to finally convince this 
Barthélémy to come to see us to discuss the price. He would come at 8 
the next morning.<br>
<br>
Later that evening Omer suggested that we he would have to inform the 
police of our presence (c'est normal!), it took us a lot of persuading 
for him not to 'give us in'. <br>
<br>
So there we were, staying in a courtyard of the mission.. with a gate 
that was so badly bend that it would no longer close. Hosted by an Abbé 
whom I did not trust (Josephine had a better feeling about him... she is
 usually right about those things). Waiting for a guy who wanted 250$US 
to ferry us across a river.<br>
<br>
Did you know that, by law, all state operated ferries in the Congo are free? Yeah right</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">Progress after day 17. Ilebo<br>
<br>


	
	
		
		
	


	<div class="lbContainer lbContainer--inline " title="" data-xf-init="lightbox" data-lb-single-image="1" data-lb-container-zoom="1" data-lb-trigger=".js-lbImage-_xfUid-2-1587032636" data-lb-id="_xfUid-2-1587032636">
		
			<div class="lbContainer-zoomer js-lbImage-_xfUid-2-1587032636" data-src="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/congo_democratic_republic_map-day17.jpg" aria-label="Zoom"></div>
		
		<img src="congo_files/congo_democratic_republic_map-day17.jpg" data-url="http://radiobaobab.be/assets/etogal/549/congo_democratic_republic_map-day17.jpg" class="bbImage" data-zoom-target="1" alt="" style="">
	</div></div><hr><div class="bbWrapper"><b>Day 18</b><br>
<br>
We got up at 7 - sleeping late! - so we would be ready to meet 
Barthélémy at 8. We felt so stupid, we should have known better. How 
lang had we been travelling trough Africa now?<br>
<br>
He showed up at 11:30.<br>
<br>
He had a bunch of official documents with him. Documents that actually 
looked legit. It described the running costs of the ferry (dated 
recently 2004 I think). And indeed, 75liters was stated as the amount of
 fuel required for a one-way trip. They would have to charge us a 
two-way trip as the boat was currently on the other side of the river, 
and they had to get it across first. Ofcourse there are no other 
passengers. There was not a lot of room for discussion there. The 50$US 
fee on the other hand was not legitimate at all, he knew it, we knew it.
 But as these guys rarely get paid by the goverment it is generally 
accepted that they ask for a fee. We got it down to a reasonable 
25$US(still too much). This would pay for the entire boat crew and they 
would 'rent' 2 batteries for us.<br>
We would buy a barrel of diesel (cheaper then per liter) and have it delivered to the port directly.<br>
<br>
We had a very long discussion about the payment, he wanted everything in
 advance as he had to pay for the diesel. We did not want to give a 
total stranger in Congo 225$US, without a contract (not that it would be
 worth anything), without having seen the boat, ... . He eventually 
agreed with a 100$US downpayment. We hoped we could trust this guy!<br>
<br>
He would cross the Kasai river tomorrow in a dug-out canoe with the boat
 crew to go and get the ferry. 'Somewhere in the afternoon' we would 
then be able to cross. <br>
<br>
I did not trust Abbé Omer. I did not trust this Barthélémy. I did not trust our deal. But we did not have a choice..</div><hr><div class="bbWrapper">The
 mission had very nice rooms on the top floor. Every room used to belong
 to a sister. With a living area, a seperate bedroom and a private 
bathroom. With bathtub and everything. The bathtub looked a bit green 
and the toilet no longer had a seat (who is this guy who keeps stealing 
all the toilet seats in Africa?). We could use one of the rooms to wash 
ourselves, but we would camp in our tent.<br>
<br>
For a minute we thought they had running water, but they hadn't. There 
is a running water system in Ilebo, but there are no meters. Instead, 
people are charged depending on how large their building is. The usual 
corruption is probably included too. The mission had a staff of 3 but 
lived in a huge house, so apparantely their water bill was huge. They 
had thus cancelled the service. According to Omer almost nobody makes 
use of the water network any longer.<br>
<br>
Instead people operate 'commercial' taps on the street. You can go there
 with a jerry can, they fill it up and you pay per liter. In a way it is
 rewarding as you first have to work a sweat before one can take a 
shower.<br>
<br>
There was another guest in the mission. A father who was asked/sponsered
 by the UN to travel around and educate people about corruption and 
long-term planning. He held a talk in the small chapel in the mission, 
we sat just outside the chapel so we could overhear everything he said. 
It was very interesting. He talked about corruption, and how it would 
make it impossible for a society to have progress. He also covered the
